  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_06a64ad6-268b-45d5-990b-adfaf7da9727'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

So, when the puppies are stolen from the Dearly home, and even Scotland Yard is unable to find them, Pongo and Missis know they must take matters into their own paws!     <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2693364495?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=classics">classics</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2693364495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12094682409113116548">I won't rate this because it's a children's book and I'm obviously not the intended audience, and I think that's a big factor in my enjoyment of this. I thought it was fun, and I could really see myself as a child LOVING it! The detailed way that the dogs think, and how the communicate would have been something my imagination would have run away with, and the grad adventure mixed with the horrible villain would have had me on the edge of my seat. As an adult, my enjoyment mostly came from imagin</span>
  <span id="freeText12094682409113116548" style="display:none">I won't rate this because it's a children's book and I'm obviously not the intended audience, and I think that's a big factor in my enjoyment of this. I thought it was fun, and I could really see myself as a child LOVING it! The detailed way that the dogs think, and how the communicate would have been something my imagination would have run away with, and the grad adventure mixed with the horrible villain would have had me on the edge of my seat. As an adult, my enjoyment mostly came from imagining how I would have reacted to it as a child, and looking forward to reading it to my kid someday. A sweet children's story for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12094682409113116548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_11533414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11533414" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/596160-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246988879p2/596160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11533414?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/596160-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">kids</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kelly by: </span>
      my grandmother
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11533414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13829040738220445116">When I was little, I got a copy of this book from my grandmother. It was old, the cover was falling off, and the edges of the pages were stained red. I adored it, and read it several times.<br/><br/>Later came the various movies, first the animated version, which was enjoyable, and then the live-action movie, which was awful. None maintained what captivated me most about the story - the inner life of the dogs and their complexity. <br/><br/>Anyway, I was suddenly seized by the need to read it again, and couldn't fi</span>
  <span id="freeText13829040738220445116" style="display:none">When I was little, I got a copy of this book from my grandmother. It was old, the cover was falling off, and the edges of the pages were stained red. I adored it, and read it several times.<br /><br />Later came the various movies, first the animated version, which was enjoyable, and then the live-action movie, which was awful. None maintained what captivated me most about the story - the inner life of the dogs and their complexity. <br /><br />Anyway, I was suddenly seized by the need to read it again, and couldn't find my old copy. It must have fallen apart beyond repair, since I certainly would never have let it go otherwise. I got a new copy and when it arrived, devoured the whole thing in one night (it was shorter than it seemed back then). <br /><br />Still a good story. Still special and to be treasured. As an adult, the datedness of the women characters (Nanny wears pants! Shocking! But she keeps the apron on, so it's ok.) which extends to the female dogs, is more troubling. Even Cruella does not ultimately have control over her life, but is trapped in the winds of change that befall her husband's career. <br /><br />Other than this, it's still a classic, and still one every kid should read (with maybe a nice chat about feminism after). </span>
  <a data-text-id="13829040738220445116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1380336989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1380336989" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380336989?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781405278409" href="/book/show/26208566-the-hundred-and-one-dalmatians">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacey by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22721588-robin-stevens">Robin Stevens</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics-challenge">classics-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380336989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer665247107337004059"><i>This post is part of the <a title='2015 Classics Challenge' href='https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/27/2015-classics-challenge/' rel='nofollow noopener'>2015 Classics Challenge</a>.</i><br/><br/><em>“Like many other much-loved humans, they believed that they owned their dogs, instead of realizing that their dogs owned them."</em><br/><br/>Cruella de Vil is enough to frighten the spots off a Dalmatian pup. But when she steals a whole family of them, the puppies’ parents, Pongo and Missus, lose no time in mounting a daring rescue mission. Will they be in time to thwart Cruella’s evil scheme, or have they bitten off more than they can chew?<br/><br/><strong>WHEN I Discovered Th</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText665247107337004059" style="display:none"><i>This post is part of the <a title="2015 Classics Challenge" href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/27/2015-classics-challenge/" rel="nofollow noopener">2015 Classics Challenge</a>.</i><br><br><em>“Like many other much-loved humans, they believed that they owned their dogs, instead of realizing that their dogs owned them."</em><br><br>Cruella de Vil is enough to frighten the spots off a Dalmatian pup. But when she steals a whole family of them, the puppies’ parents, Pongo and Missus, lose no time in mounting a daring rescue mission. Will they be in time to thwart Cruella’s evil scheme, or have they bitten off more than they can chew?<br><br><strong>WHEN I Discovered This Classic</strong><br>Likely when I first watched the Disney adaptation in the 90s. I'm much more of a cat person, but I've always loved the film and adored Dalmatians!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453740396ra/17865485.gif" alt="101" width="500" height="368" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>WHY I Chose to Read It </strong><br>You picked my December classic and <i>The Hundred and One Dalmatians</i> won (27.32% of the vote). It was included in the poll because I wanted to read this newly-published edition, illustrated by Alex T. Smith.<br><br><strong>WHAT Makes It A Classic</strong><br>It is written by <em>I Capture the Castle</em> author Dodie Smith, a much-loved children's classic and author.<br><br><strong>WHAT I Thought of This Classic</strong><br>I was hooked on <em>The Hundred and One Dalmatians</em> from the beginning. I loved discovering all the little differences from the story I grew up with and was surprised to discover that our courageous couple is not Pongo and Perdita, but Pongo and Missus. I was pleased to see that all of the animals in the story still had distinct, lovable personalities.<br><br><em>The Hundred and One Dalmatians</em> is written in a wonderful style. It's told almost conversationally, and in a way that is incredibly enjoyable to follow. I read it as if I were floating down a calm river or on a quiet jaunt through the countryside. But combined with the tense – and at times quite frightening – scenes that make Cruella de Vil one of the most notable villains in children's literature, it becomes a brilliant canine adventure. It's also beautifully accompanied by Alex T. Smith's gorgeous illustrations, particularly of the puppies!<br><br>Even though I adored the story, I was a little disappointed by the attitude towards some of the female characters and the perpetuation of traditional gender roles, even if it <em>was</em> originally published 60 years ago. I was also intrigued by the description of Cruella de Vil (“She had a dark skin, black eyes with a tinge of red in them, and a very pointed nose.") compared to how she's usually imagined – as a lady with pale skin. If you Google 'Cruella de Vil' and 'dark skin', you get zero results. Why is this?<br><br>Even if a little old-fashioned at times, <em>The Hundred and One Dalmatians</em> is still an incredibly charming classic that I thoroughly enjoyed. It was a delightful end to the <a href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/27/2015-classics-challenge/" rel="nofollow noopener">2015 Classics Challenge</a>.<br><br><em>"Nanny Cook slept dreaming of Dalmatian puppies dressed as babies, and Nanny Butler slept dreaming of babies dresses as Dalmatian puppies."</em><br><br><strong>WILL It Stay A Classic</strong><br>It's difficult to think of the book without thinking of the film. Would it still be a classic without Disney?<br><br><strong>WHO I’d Recommend It To</strong><br>People who love illustrated fiction, puppies and children's books.<br><br><em>“Dogs can never speak the language of humans, and humans can never speak the language of dogs. But many dogs can understand almost every word humans say, while humans seldom learn to recognize more than half a dozen barks, if that.”</em><br><br><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="665247107337004059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3162640390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3162640390" />
    <a title="MissBecka Gee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5997380-missbecka-gee"><img alt="MissBecka Gee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544171422p2/5997380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3162640390?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MissBecka Gee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MissBecka Gee" href="/user/show/5997380-missbecka-gee">MissBecka Gee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22729476-one-hundred-and-one-dalmatians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5997380-missbecka-gee?shelf=2020-books-i-read">2020-books-i-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5997380-missbecka-gee?shelf=our-home-library">our-home-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5997380-missbecka-gee?shelf=storytime-with-daniel">storytime-with-daniel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3162640390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16949361339244284846"><b>Update:</b><br/>Finally got around to re-watching the movie and while I enjoyed it and will likely watch it again in the future...the book is a better fit for me.<br/><br/><b>Original Review:</b><br/>That was certainly a lot darker (and funnier) than what I remember from the Disney version.<br/>Also I feel like a lot of this was changed for the movie. <br/>It's been too long since I've seen it to be sure.<br/>We are gonna re-watch the movie tonight for comparison.<br/>Not sure if my husband and I will bother with the "sequel" book since it looks</span>
  <span id="freeText16949361339244284846" style="display:none"><b>Update:</b><br />Finally got around to re-watching the movie and while I enjoyed it and will likely watch it again in the future...the book is a better fit for me.<br /><br /><b>Original Review:</b><br />That was certainly a lot darker (and funnier) than what I remember from the Disney version.<br />Also I feel like a lot of this was changed for the movie. <br />It's been too long since I've seen it to be sure.<br />We are gonna re-watch the movie tonight for comparison.<br />Not sure if my husband and I will bother with the "sequel" book since it looks like it has the barest connection with this one.</span>

<div id="review_281862571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281862571" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4778766-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294588675p2/4778766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281862571?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/4778766-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281862571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2795153272518705584">A delightful children's book that I read as a kid (many times) and haven't read since. I decided to read it again to see if it held up and was still fun. It definitely was an entertaining read.<br/><br/>When I was looking it up, I was surprised to see so many Goodreads reviews complaining of sexism or anti-feminine views presented in the book. This was certainly never anything I noticed as a kid, but then, how many kids are clued in to that sort of thing? I found myself reading to enjoy, and also to exami</span>
  <span id="freeText2795153272518705584" style="display:none">A delightful children's book that I read as a kid (many times) and haven't read since. I decided to read it again to see if it held up and was still fun. It definitely was an entertaining read.<br /><br />When I was looking it up, I was surprised to see so many Goodreads reviews complaining of sexism or anti-feminine views presented in the book. This was certainly never anything I noticed as a kid, but then, how many kids are clued in to that sort of thing? I found myself reading to enjoy, and also to examine, and my findings are that this book is hardly demeaning of women.<br /><br />To be clear, I mostly focused on gender roles and the differences portrayed between the sexes, and judged the book thereby.<br /><br />What first caught my attention was the fact that Mr. Dearly was the primary caregiver to the newborn dalmatian puppies (beyond their mother, Missis). He crawls into the cupboard for two days feeding babies constantly while working long distance over the phone. If traditional gender roles were in play, shouldn't this be Mrs. Dearly's job? This is clearly an inversion of the binary. Secondarily, of the two female nannies, Nanny Butler insists on wearing pants after the Dearlys are married, and back when this written, this was hardly the social norm. Again, a seeming inversion of the stereotype.<br /><br />What I looked at next was the differences between Pongo and Missis. Pongo can understand human speech, can read, and thinks faster and clearer than Missis. On a cursory reading, it does appear that Pongo is presented as superior, and Missis as inferior, but that isn't the case. It is a clearly established conceit throughout the book that dogs differ in intelligence, and in human understanding. It is quite clearly stated that Pongo played with alphabet blocks and volumes of Shakespeare (thus accounting for his English comprehension) and is even referred to as the "keenest mind in all of dogdom" which establishes his special peculiarity in both intelligence and human understanding. If one considers that a dog learns English much as any other non-native English speaker, this lines up exactly with human experience and is not sexist at all. After all, how much English would you learn if the most common word you heard was your name, and the rest was in condescending baby talk? Probably not even as much as Missis. Also, she clearly seems to be personally disinterested: she simply does not bother or care to learn more, which is a personal choice.<br /><br />Now, one could make a case for sexism based on the fact that it is Pongo to whom these advantages are given and not to Missis, and if all the dominant traits were Pongo's, I would agree with you, but in almost all other cases, the two dogs are equal. They share equal affection and concern for one another. They equally adopt and feel ownership for all of the other dalmatian puppies, they are equal in their strength and determination throughout their desperate journey. In fact, Missis even trumps Pongo when he is injured by the little boy who throws things. She restrains him from acting against the child in anger; she finds the haystack and forces him to rest; she finds the Spaniel and secures food and lodging for them both. Again, if this were clearly sexist, he would be rescuing her instead of the other way around. In this episode, she is the hero, not the male dog.<br /><br />There is one episode with the Spaniel in which Missis tries to learn her right from her left and ends up horribly confused and unable to get the two straight, and that could be seen as an indication that the female possess less intelligence, but abstract concepts are hard to grasp for someone that isn't introduced to them from a young age. I am a male, and I am an adult, and I frequently have trouble telling my right from my left. This is humiliating to admit, but it is true. I never bothered to learn them when I was a child, and as an adult, the concept is more difficult to grasp. There is clear research showing that much learning is cemented in the early ages, and the brain becomes more rigid after that. I have managed to decrease my ambiguity about right and left, but it has taken practice and focus. In the story, Missis has much more on her mind, and is clearly emotionally stressed about both her husband and her puppies. It is no wonder, then, that during the heat of the moment she simply became frustrated and couldn't grasp the concept. Again, why her and not Pongo? Again, I think this is part of staying consistent to character rather than making a sexist statement about the inferiority of women. If anything, Missis' lack of education is more Mrs. Dearly's fault that her own for not providing her with Shakespeare to chew on, but then while Mr. Dearly is given barely a few sentences to round out his job and life, we are given almost nothing about Mrs. Dearly. This is, after all, a story about the dogs and not their pets, and so there is precious little from which to draw conclusions. In order to remain un-sexist, one does not have to always choose the female over the male, but must show equality and fair treatment. In all, Missis is Pongo's equal in practically every way that matters. I get the feeling that if Pongo chose to teach her, Missis would learn quite aptly.<br /><br />Lastly, some people got upset about the fact that the one puppy who was obsessed with television was the youngest female puppy, Cadpig, who was also the weakest, and they called this sexist. I disagree. In fact, this lone, apparently weak female made for Dodie Smith (the author) the most important observation of all. The narrator of the story, not necessarily Smith, appears to be religious. The last building in which the puppies take refuge is a church. Cadpig becomes more obsessed with the nativity on display than she ever was with the television. In the end, she concludes that whoever "owned [the church] - someone very kind she was sure" had set out that refuge for them, complete with puppy sized beds. Clearly she is misinterpreting the reality of a church, as only a young, uneducated puppy can (female or male) but the narrator is using her to make a statement about God: the kindest person who looks out for even the most lost and destitute soul, according to most Christian theologies anyway. It is not insignificant, then, that the smallest and weakest character, through her obsession to the television, is the only one to realize the ultimate reality of good triumphing over the "de Vil". To the woman is given the realization of the theme, plot, and message of the entire story.<br /><br />Sexist? hardly. if it were, it would be Pongo making that realization. There is every indication that he missed the implication entirely.<br /><br />Actually, for my own part, I thought that having the villain of the story be a woman, the colorful and deliciously evil Cruella de Vil, could possibly be the strongest argument made for sexism. After all, the woman is the evil one! However, as Cruella's cat explains, her husband was no less evil, just weaker, and in that is the deconstruction of the argument: Cruella is the villain because she is much stronger than her husband, who is made out to be a mostly sympathetic character until his true nature is revealed.<br /><br />Therefore, between Mr. Dearly inverting the nurturing paradigm, Missis heroically saving her husband, Cadpig realizing the moral of the story, and Cruella trumping her husband's strength, this book is not sexist in the least. At least, in my humble opinion. Read it with an open mind, divorcing yourself of pre-conceived ideas and agendas and decide for yourself.<br /><br />Over all the book was entertaining, amusing, fun, and quite well written for what is essentially a children's novel. As much as I enjoyed it as a kid, I enjoyed it probably just as much as an adult.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2795153272518705584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer3039764839782218741">The part of this book I liked best was the Starlight Barking. Since reading it at age 9 or so, I have observed the phenomenon innumerable times. It's comforting to know what the dogs are really doing. Thank you, Dodie Smith, for explaining it so well.<br/><br/>Three or four years ago, while I was living in Sunnyvale, I saw a remarkable example of how useful the Starlight Barking can be. My friend Beth Ann has two very smart Dobermanns. Late one evening, both of them suddenly started yelping furiously, for</span>
  <span id="freeText3039764839782218741" style="display:none">The part of this book I liked best was the Starlight Barking. Since reading it at age 9 or so, I have observed the phenomenon innumerable times. It's comforting to know what the dogs are really doing. Thank you, Dodie Smith, for explaining it so well.<br /><br />Three or four years ago, while I was living in Sunnyvale, I saw a remarkable example of how useful the Starlight Barking can be. My friend Beth Ann has two very smart Dobermanns. Late one evening, both of them suddenly started yelping furiously, for no apparent reason. We could just about hear that the mutt next door was also expressing concern. Luckily, Beth Ann is quite fluent in Dog, and knew that she needed to go outside to see what was up. She immediately smelled smoke. The house two doors down was on fire! She called the fire brigade, and, literally within five minutes, we had three giant fire trucks parked outside, blocking the whole street. The dogs looked pleased with the effect their warning had had.<br /><br />As one does, we went out again to gawp. It wasn't actually that dramatic - the house in question was empty, so no one had to go in and perform a rescue. While we were watching, our neighbor stumbled out of his front door in a bathrobe, looking very sleepy and confused. "Oh... right! So <i>that's</i> why Gromit was so agitated! I see!" He was clearly rather less fluent than Beth Ann.<br /></span>

    <a title="Mackey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28470777-mackey"><img alt="Mackey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562878870p2/28470777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer142530242568843805">I saw this as a "classic read" and realized that it was yet another book that I never marked as "read." <br/><br/>This was, hands down, one of my kids' favorite books. If you've only ever seen the Disney movies then you definitely should give this book a read. It is a bit different from Disney's version - aren't they always - but the repetitiveness and alliteration in the book make it a delight for children. There is a reason it is a "classic." </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12522228320840986554">I loved this audiobook experience with this classic. My brother loves the Disney movie so I’ve always known about the book, but hadn’t been super interested in reading it as I felt I already knew the story. I was wrong, and offer my apologies to Dodie Smith. Her writing drew me in and kept my attention throughout the book. The plot isn' exactly the same as Disney is known to change things and they definitely did for this book. Even though I grew up with the movie, I greatly prefer the book over </span>
  <span id="freeText12522228320840986554" style="display:none">I loved this audiobook experience with this classic. My brother loves the Disney movie so I’ve always known about the book, but hadn’t been super interested in reading it as I felt I already knew the story. I was wrong, and offer my apologies to Dodie Smith. Her writing drew me in and kept my attention throughout the book. The plot isn' exactly the same as Disney is known to change things and they definitely did for this book. Even though I grew up with the movie, I greatly prefer the book over the movie. In the future, I'm going to look into her other works because I was hooked throughout the book. I ended up buying my own audio copy so I can enjoy the story anytime I want. The narrator was the perfect choice. He added some liveliness and sensitivity that was required for some of the character's and iciness that goes with Cruella.</span>

  <span id="freeText9346742512237288942" style="display:none">Look, I have nothing against Disney. Their movies are fun and entertaining. But I just wish maybe they would give more credit to the original works that inspired them for their stories. Most people I know don't even realize that so many of their movies are based on actual books. Really, really good books.<br /><br />I mean, Perdita doesn't even show up until maybe chapter 3, and she is NOT Pongo's wife. His wife's name is Missus. Why did they have to cut out Missus, that brave soul? Poor Missus. She's adorable:<br />"I'm not very good at right and left," said Missis, "especially left."<br />The Spaniel smiled, then looked at her paws. "This will help you," he said. "That paw with the pretty spot -- that is your right paw."<br />"Then which is my left paw?"<br />"Why, the other paw, of course."<br />"Back or front?" asked Missis.<br />"Just forget your back paws."<br />Missis was puzzled. Could she forget her back paws? And if she could, would it be safe? <br />...<br />Just before they reached the kitchen garden, Missis said, "Pongo, do dogs have spots on their right paws or on their left paws?"<br />"That depends on the dog," said Pongo.<br />Missis shook her head. "It's hopeless," she thought. "How can I depend on a thing that depends?"<br />...<br />The Spaniel noticed her dazed look and said playfully, "Now which is your right paw?"<br />"One of the front ones," said Missis brightly."<br /><br />"So Mr. Dearly rang up the Splendid Vet, who was delighted to be waked up and called out at nearly midnight on Christmas Eve."<br /><br />"How was anyone to guess that this playful creature owned one of the keenest brains in Dogdom? It was at work now. All through the long December night he put two and two together and made four. Once or twice he almost made five."<br /><br />Such a classic. You should read it.</span>

<div id="review_2013345585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2013345585" />
    <a title="Karen Witzler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2125591-karen-witzler"><img alt="Karen Witzler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427207218p2/2125591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2013345585?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Witzler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Witzler" href="/user/show/2125591-karen-witzler">Karen Witzler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780749702045" href="/book/show/1230557.The_Hundred_and_One_Dalmatians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2125591-karen-witzler?shelf=childrens-classics">childrens-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013345585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6118544179465484173">Read aloud to me on late spring evenings by my nostalgic nineteen year old daughter - this is NOT the Disney version. Completely charming with a Beatrix Potteresque realism added to the animal characterizations of Pongo and Missis...and Perdita, who is quite a different character from the film version. This makes a wonderful read-aloud and many children would enjoy it, however --- Cruella de Vil is truly evil and her casual talk of drowning many kittens and pups would be disturbing to many moder</span>
  <span id="freeText6118544179465484173" style="display:none">Read aloud to me on late spring evenings by my nostalgic nineteen year old daughter - this is NOT the Disney version. Completely charming with a Beatrix Potteresque realism added to the animal characterizations of Pongo and Missis...and Perdita, who is quite a different character from the film version. This makes a wonderful read-aloud and many children would enjoy it, however --- Cruella de Vil is truly evil and her casual talk of drowning many kittens and pups would be disturbing to many modern families. Parents are strongly cautioned, but the high quality of the writing makes me hope that The Hundred and One Dalmatians will continue to find an audience. ( I'll wager it's been purged from many libraries though for the above reasons.) The history of the Dalmation breed is interwoven with the story and Dodie Smith's fine writing makes it read smooth as silk. The English village dogs who assist Pongo and Missis in their quest to save their family are finely rendered - I loved the spaniel, daughter loved the retrievers and the Staffordshire terrier (who knows just what ought to be done with Cruella). A wonderful book and I look forward to the further adventures of the Cadpig in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31964.The_Starlight_Barking__The_Hundred_and_One_Dalmatians___2_" title="The Starlight Barking (The Hundred and One Dalmatians, #2) by Dodie Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starlight Barking</a>. ---- If you think you know this story , but do not know the Cadpig, you've not read the original.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6118544179465484173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9335363684953133641" style="display:none">Man I absolutely loved this Disney movie growing up, so I was completely shocked that there was a book! Then we meet the incredible and super evil Cruella de Vil, who is still wanting all the puppies. <br /><br />In the end, I really enjoyed all the characters and the entire storyline. <div id="review_102175519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102175519" />
    <a title="Jet Silver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2683477-jet-silver"><img alt="Jet Silver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263079716p2/2683477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102175519?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jet Silver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jet Silver" href="/user/show/2683477-jet-silver">Jet Silver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405224802" href="/book/show/885910.The_Hundred_and_One_Dalmatians">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2683477-jet-silver?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2683477-jet-silver?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102175519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2414446931097677957">This was one of the most sexist books I have ever read. Worse, I first read it when I was ten or so and didn't notice the sexism, which means that its ridiculous list of 'male' and 'female' attributes went into my psyche unchallenged. <br/><br/>According to Dodie Smith, men and male dogs are stronger, don't feel the cold, understand both numbers and words better, have a sense of direction, possess deductive powers, are inventive, loyal and brave. <br/><br/>Women and female dogs can't tell their left from their righ</span>
  <span id="freeText2414446931097677957" style="display:none">This was one of the most sexist books I have ever read. Worse, I first read it when I was ten or so and didn't notice the sexism, which means that its ridiculous list of 'male' and 'female' attributes went into my psyche unchallenged. <br /><br />According to Dodie Smith, men and male dogs are stronger, don't feel the cold, understand both numbers and words better, have a sense of direction, possess deductive powers, are inventive, loyal and brave. <br /><br />Women and female dogs can't tell their left from their right after a page of instruction in how to do so, feel proud of not getting lost while heading in a straight line, can't count - even one's own puppies, don't understand either human or dog speech as well as a male dog, get tired about four times as fast as male puppies, are jealous, vain, proud of their clothes, are hysterical, silly, distracted, and generally ridiculous. But they are <i>pretty</i>. <br /><br />What a steaming pile of crap. <br /><br />Also, there's a scene of "thieving gypsies", and one can speak either Romany or "normal". Ugh. <br /><br />I really wanted to like this. It's a charming story, in parts. But it is choc full of blatant, unchecked sexism, and I am boggled that Disney seems to have done a better job than the source. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2414446931097677957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3948322" />
    <a title="D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70408-d"><img alt="D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1186154184p2/70408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who wants a brilliant, brilliant read</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70408-d?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70408-d?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70408-d?shelf=classic-canon-influential">classic-canon-influential</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70408-d?shelf=childrens-lit-picture-book">childrens-lit-picture-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3948322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6597563460816198721">*** ORIGINAL REVIEW -- August 1, 2007 ***<br/>O happy day when during a free-reading period in Mrs. Chismar's fifth-grade class I opened an old, dog-eared (as it were) edition of this masterpiece. Smith's ability to evoke a scene and pen enchanting but vulnerable characters earns her a place among the greats. The image of the ancient colonel sharing tea with his Old English Sheepdog in their sound Suffolk country home before a crackling fire on a stormy night is my standard for domestic comfort (Mmm,</span>
  <span id="freeText6597563460816198721" style="display:none">*** ORIGINAL REVIEW -- August 1, 2007 ***<br />O happy day when during a free-reading period in Mrs. Chismar's fifth-grade class I opened an old, dog-eared (as it were) edition of this masterpiece. Smith's ability to evoke a scene and pen enchanting but vulnerable characters earns her a place among the greats. The image of the ancient colonel sharing tea with his Old English Sheepdog in their sound Suffolk country home before a crackling fire on a stormy night is my standard for domestic comfort (Mmm, hot buttered toast). I have only read two works by Smith---this and <i>I Capture the Castle</i>---and both are brilliant, brilliant works. Yes, her former story has been appropriated (and deftly exploited) by Disney, but why is the original---why aren't <i>all</i> of her writings---more visible? She masters the pen, people. If anyone knows how to get ahold of a copy with the original artwork, CALL ME!<br /><br />*** UPDATED REVIEW -- September 6, 2010 ***<br />listened to a nicely narrated audio version. this time through, i was struck by the casually received misogyny and the enforced, strict gender roles throughout. i still quite enjoy the story, but getting to know dodie smith's oeuvre better over the years, i can't say i'm surprised by this; she internalized QUITE a bit of gendered ick.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6597563460816198721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8895002952845236354">As weird as it sounds, this was the first time I read this book. I read the Disney version when I was a kid but this one was so much better! The dogs felt like real characters and they were so sassy and independent! I loved reading about their adventures around England. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_23484247" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23484247" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/954812-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1279752265p2/954812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23484247?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/954812-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/954812-heather?shelf=mady-and-me-books">mady-and-me-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23484247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14198348753420585493">Oh the joy of it. I don't remember seeing the movie as a kid (though I'm told it's the very first movie I ever saw, at a drive-in, at age 4...!) But I vividly remember reading the book when I was in 4th or 5th grade and just loving it. And I wasn't even a "dog person" as a kid (or as an adult, until the past year or so). <br/><br/>Anyway we read it aloud as a chapter book for bedtime last week and it was just as terrific as I remembered. The story is so delightfully British... there is something about the</span>
  <span id="freeText14198348753420585493" style="display:none">Oh the joy of it. I don't remember seeing the movie as a kid (though I'm told it's the very first movie I ever saw, at a drive-in, at age 4...!) But I vividly remember reading the book when I was in 4th or 5th grade and just loving it. And I wasn't even a "dog person" as a kid (or as an adult, until the past year or so). <br /><br />Anyway we read it aloud as a chapter book for bedtime last week and it was just as terrific as I remembered. The story is so delightfully British... there is something about the narrative voice that reminds me of Dorothy Sayers (!!) but relishing the diversity of dog personalities rather than regions and classes... and there's also a post-WWII sensibility about the keen brains and willing spirits and good hearts of British Dogdom coming together to rescue the puppies. I love the Twilight Barking network (and the way the dogs refer to it as being "on the barking," like being on the 'phone...). <br /><br />There are surprisingly moving cameos for dogs like the gallant old spaniel and his "pet" Sir Charles who thinks that Pongo and Missis are ghosts of dalmatians he knew as a child, and the "feather-brained as well as feather-tailed" Irish Setter, and the hearty pipe-smoking Staffordshire Terrier in the moving van, and the Christmas Eve episode where the puppies briefly take refuge in an Anglican church... none of these made it into the Disney movie and they're just so beautiful.<br /><br />My only quibble with this edition is the illustrations, which are okay but a) there aren't enough of them (the original edition had small or large ink drawing adorning every page, in the style of the Winnie the Pooh books) and b) there's a picture of Cruella that's so ugly and scary that Madeleine made me fold the page over! If you read the book, Cruella isn't described as old or ugly... she's glamorous, young (the same age as newly-wed Mrs Dearly), and bohemian-decadent. Again, like something out of Dorothy Sayers. Or maybe Evelyn Waugh.<br /><br />Another bedtime winner!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14198348753420585493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6508398978543284750" style="display:none">Such a nostalgic, delightful read!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469535871ra/19827843.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Glen Close as Cruella de Vil was a highlight of my childhood.</i> <br><br>To be clear the story is actually about a family whose dalmatian pups have been stolen in order to make a fur coat and of course, I'm aware that justice needed to be served to the perpetrator. But what I fell in love with as a child was the absolute crazy that is <i>Devil Woman</i>. <br><br>The gender politics of this book are exactly what I expect from a novel written in the 1950s. Even if our heroes are dogs, Missis is angel of the home type, but a ditz and Pongo is patriarch, gentle and a little too patronizing for my modern sensibilities. That being said, the pair complements each other's strengths and further the rescue mission at crucial points. The puppies were cute. There was a happy ending, bla, bla bla, back to Cruella.<br><br>What initially drew me in was the amazing <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KcdQk7JBPzQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruella De Vil (Disney Original Song)</a> and I think because of it, I read this book 8 or 9 years ago. In the 1996 live-action remake, Cruella is a fashion diva with a murderous streak and I just could not look away. This book however is a little more mean spirited towards Cruella and there's not a lot of her in it. There are a lot of people and dogs talking about her and fearing her and her affinity for fur and pepper. I wish there were more of her, but I'm sure she must have been busy running her fashion line with her incompetent husband. <br><br>Miss Cruella, could I give you some advice?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469536424ra/19827948.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer618487696483298249">I absolutely love this book. Years after first reading it, I still pull it out for perusal or rereading. My version has different illustrations (and I am obsessed with only ever reading that copy; the illustrations are brilliant), one of my favorites being of the pups in the church.<br/><br/>And I still, to this day, quote dear Missus: "How can I depend on something that depends?"<br/><br/>Reread in January 2020:<br/><br/><br/>I had not reread this in several years.   <span id="freeText618487696483298249" style="display:none">I absolutely love this book. Years after first reading it, I still pull it out for perusal or rereading. My version has different illustrations (and I am obsessed with only ever reading that copy; the illustrations are brilliant), one of my favorites being of the pups in the church.<br /><br />And I still, to this day, quote dear Missus: "How can I depend on something that depends?"<br /><br />Reread in January 2020:<br /><br /><br />I had not reread this in several years. I hate the blatant racism/sexism. I definitely wouldn't recommend to a lot of people, at least without being clear about the contents.<br /><br />No group should be portrayed this way, especially in children's books.<br /><br />I still love the story, Cadpig, in her little cart or sitting in the church, just makes me cry, but this was a difficult reread.<br />Thankfully, if I go to do another one, I'll know what in getting into.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3211825356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3211825356" />
    <a title="Mathew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42270985-mathew"><img alt="Mathew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554409562p2/42270985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3211825356?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mathew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mathew" href="/user/show/42270985-mathew">Mathew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=abusive-adults">abusive-adults</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=working-together">working-together</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=gypsies">gypsies</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3211825356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14172378862852700876">By the time she had begun writing, Dodie Smith was already a celebrated playwright. According to a review, the idea for this particular story came from when a friend commented on how Dodie Smith's own dalmations would look wonderful as a coat (in jest of course!). And so, Cruella de Vil, and her passion for furs, was born alongside Pongo, Missis and the tribe at large. <br/><br/>A rescue story told from the point of view of the dogs (a far cry from the canine-narrated <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/945522.Fire__Bed__and_Bone' title='Fire, Bed, and Bone by Henrietta Branford' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fire, Bed, and Bone</a>), this whole stor</span>
  <span id="freeText14172378862852700876" style="display:none">By the time she had begun writing, Dodie Smith was already a celebrated playwright. According to a review, the idea for this particular story came from when a friend commented on how Dodie Smith's own dalmations would look wonderful as a coat (in jest of course!). And so, Cruella de Vil, and her passion for furs, was born alongside Pongo, Missis and the tribe at large. <br /><br />A rescue story told from the point of view of the dogs (a far cry from the canine-narrated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/945522.Fire__Bed__and_Bone" title="Fire, Bed, and Bone by Henrietta Branford" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire, Bed, and Bone</a>), this whole story was a speedy delight and, save for the staple, dated gypsy encounter, will still win over young and old hearts alike. For me, it is all the canine perceptions of people and the characteristics of the different breeds that I loved as well as Pongo and Missis' journey to and from London to save their pups. </span>

<div id="review_16560673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16560673" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/913232-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214915538p2/913232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16560673?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/913232-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380459711" href="/book/show/511617.The_Hundred_And_One_Dalmatians">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer16560673&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16560673" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1473093444295341818"> Again, not Disney - but a very lovely book! The story of Pongo and Missis ("a young married couple of Dalmatians"); their devoted pets, the Dearlys; household helpers Nanny Cook and Nanny Butler; the Pongos' fifteen beloved young puppies; and Perdita, the former stray and devoted foster mother who's also a Dalmatian, is told in enchanting detail. When the puppies are kidnapped by the unspeakably evil Cruella de Vil, the fur-fanatic wife of a furrier who desires - and fully intends to acquire - </span>
  <span id="freeText1473093444295341818" style="display:none"> Again, not Disney - but a very lovely book! The story of Pongo and Missis ("a young married couple of Dalmatians"); their devoted pets, the Dearlys; household helpers Nanny Cook and Nanny Butler; the Pongos' fifteen beloved young puppies; and Perdita, the former stray and devoted foster mother who's also a Dalmatian, is told in enchanting detail. When the puppies are kidnapped by the unspeakably evil Cruella de Vil, the fur-fanatic wife of a furrier who desires - and fully intends to acquire - a Dalmatian-skin coat, Pongo and Missis must travel cross-country from London to Suffolk, making many new friends and encountering many perils along the way. The dogs find their pups still alive and well, imprisoned in Hell Hall, the de Vils' ancestral house; they also find that the situation is much more complicated - and the immediate danger much greater - than anticipated. Can Pongo, "the keenest brain in Dogdom", lead his family safely home? A must-read! Incidentally, this book also saved a life! In the chapter which covered the puppies' birth, Mr. Dearly uses a towel to massage and stimulate the blood flow in a stillborn puppy, reviving her faint heartbeat and bringing her back to life (she survived, and turned out to be one of the best of the puppies). Many years later, I tried the same method with a stillborn kitten. It worked!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1473093444295341818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k+Pf7vQ43diiWL6mbvjS6N7/Wdj2ZxKb4SQ5BcvxLWShqmulPACiGvT3TUGgUe059b2oLmcH3ZF1mffESKMxPA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('05CSsBJPMZVPKdZKlRs+msOd4wSiSduTIDXWs7tiphXh2Sb72ndOVxmGJa1bsgFL6N8S8jMpFJm0iBhyODC6TQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11321241990048936615">Born Dorothy Gladys Smith in Lancashire, England, Dodie Smith was raised in Manchester (her memoir is titled <i>A Childhood in Manchester</i>). She was just an infant when her father died, and she grew up fatherless until age 14, when her mother remarried and the family moved to London. There she studied at the Royal Academy of Dramatic Arts and tried for a career as an actress, but with little success. </span>
  <span id="freeText11321241990048936615" style="display:none">Born Dorothy Gladys Smith in Lancashire, England, Dodie Smith was raised in Manchester (her memoir is titled <i>A Childhood in Manchester</i>). She was just an infant when her father died, and she grew up fatherless until age 14, when her mother remarried and the family moved to London. There she studied at the Royal Academy of Dramatic Arts and tried for a career as an actress, but with little success. She finally wound up taking a job as a toy buyer for a furniture store to make ends meet. Giving up dreams of an acting career, she turned to writing plays, and in 1931 her first play, <i>Autumn Crocus</i>, was published (under the pseudonym “C.L. Anthony”). It was a success, and her story — from failed actress to furniture store employee to successful writer — captured the imagination of the public and she was featured in papers all over the country. Although she could now afford to move to a London townhouse, she didn't get caught up in the “literary” scene — she married a man who was a fellow employee at the furniture store.<br /><br />During World War II she and her husband moved to the United States, mostly because of his stand as a conscientious objector and the social and legal difficulties that entailed. She was still homesick for England, though, as reflected in her first novel, <i>I Capture the Castle</i> (1948). During her stay she formed close friendships with such authors as Christopher Isherwood and John Van Druten, and was aided in her literary endeavors by writer A.J. Cronin.<br /><br />She is perhaps best known for her novel <i>The Hundred and One Dalmatians</i>, a hugely popular childrens book that has been made into a string of very successful animated films by Walt Disney. She died in 1990.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11321241990048936615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
